  40. The manual says to use this product exclusively for 21 days to give your face time to adapt to the shaving system. For users like me, this is an unforgivably long grace period. A well-engineered razor should adapt to your face. Your face should not have to adapt to the razor. I was disappointed from the very first shave and after a few more shaving attempts, abandoned it to go back to disposables. With every single shave, I had to clean up strays with a disposable, especially around the neck and under the chin. But in order to write a fair review, I started using it again 2 wks ago and decided to complete the 21 day trial.<br /><br />After these 2 new weeks, I continue to be disappointed. This razor under-performs compared to other electrics I've used in the past. I'm not a hairy guy but my facial hair does grow back fast, requiring a quick shave every 2 days. If my facial hair grew just slightly longer (3-4 days), the \\"lift and cut\\" system becomes an irritating \\"yank and cut\\" system. The motor is either not fast enough or not powerful enough to keep pace as I roll the razor across my face. This was never a problem with past electrics I've owned, like the Remington Microscreen product line. Norelco's triple head design here add nothing to the functionality, and in fact, detract from the shaving performance in a major way.<br /><br />The \\"Patented Reflex Action System\\" which was supposed to adjust \\"automatically to every curve on your face and neck for an uncommonly smooth shave\\" did not adjust to mine at all. Shaving with this takes me a lot longer and requires more effort than with a manual razor or my old Remington. The entire reason is the small active surface area of the heads. The actual cutting zone is a very small target consisting of only the outer ring of each circular head, which hair must poke itself through in order to get cut. As you pass the razor over your face, the hair must hit one of these small sweet-spots to get lifted and cut away. Every other part of the razor's face besides the rings is simply a dead-weight non-cutting surface, resulting in a lot of missed hairs whether using straight strokes or circular motions. The Remingtons, by contrast, offer a wide horizontal head with a lot of active surface area and requires much fewer strokes across the face.<br /><br />The few design aspects I did like:<br /><br />- elastic bungee cord plug minimizes entanglement and accidents<br />- flip-out sideburns trimmer works, though also small surface area<br />- rubberized non-slip grip<br /><br />I will continue the experiment for 1 more wk, as the manual instructs and update as needed. I am not impressed so far.<br /><br />UPDATE: Nov 27, 2009: I continue to be frustrated by this razor's performance. It's simply not a good product.'s face besides the rings is simply a dead-weight non-cutting surface, resulting in a lot of missed hairs whether using straight strokes or circular motions. The Remingtons, by contrast, offer a wide horizontal head with a lot of active surface area and requires much fewer strokes across the face. I am not impressed so far. UPDATE: Nov 27, 2009: I continue to be frustrated by this razor's performance. It's simply not a good product.

With older models, you could even out the wear on the three cutters by snapping this assembly back on in a different orientation after cleaning, since it was rotationally symmetrical. With the 6940LC, you can't do this... you'd have to disassemble and move the three cutting heads manually. Looks to me like someone introduced this hassle to hopefully sell more blades...<br /><br />As others have noted, the cord is a little too short, and this shaver is WAY overpackaged in both a box and multiple layers of tough, molded plastic that have to be carefully cut apart with box cutters.

  71. A feature of electric shavers that razors do not have is that they will lift hairs out of their follicles to cut the hairs, resulting in a hair cut short enough that it is below the skin layer afterwards (Lift and Cut feature is what it is called for Norelcos). If done right, an electric razor can offer a closer shave than a razor, but you will lose skin due to its use (obviously). I have to say my new 6940LC offers an incredible shave for a bargain price; compared to my previous use of Gillette Fusion razors, the Norelco 6940LC offers a much easier and closer shave. Getting the sides of the chin with a razor is hard as hell, but the 6940LC takes care out that easily. Make sure your facial hair area has been warmed with hot water (such as after a shower) to relax the skin and hair follices, shave with the 6940LC, throw some cold water on your face so that the skin and follicles contract, and voila. Super-duper shave that is as good or better than a razor. Make sure you clean your blades regularly with some shaver lubricant (such as Remington Shaver Saver), and you will get an awesome shave every time. One day I hope to get a premium electric shaver (such as the Braun 790cc Pulsonic), but this is awesome for the price. Plus, you will not have any problems with batteries or charges because it is a wall plug shaver. No batteries, no problem, no facial hair!

  116. I've waited about 6 months to write a review, because IMO you can't judge an electric shaver until that amount of time has gone by (well you can, if the thing just doesn't work at all from day one, but if it does, you have to see how long it will last).<br /><br />I'm very pleased with this shaver! No, it will not give you as close a shave as a good blade or a $200 shaver, but it gives a damn good shave and the price can't be beat. And after 6 months, it is still shaving as good as on day one, important because replacement heads are as expensive as the shaver itself.<br /><br />One drawback: This shaver has poor shavings 'ventilation'. Your shaved hairs will accumulate very quickly inside the head. I recommend removing the screens and brushing the blades every 3-4 shaves, otherwise the heads get clogged and shaving closeness diminishes. This sounds onerous but it isn't, since thanks to the design of the head, it is extremely easy and quick to do. Not a hassle at all.<br /><br />Finally, this is CRITICAL: On the inside of each screen, there is a center dimple where the blade fits. Hairs will gradually wrap themselves around this dimple and they are very hard to see. When this happens, the shaver will work BARELY AT ALL, as the wrapped-around hairs will reduce blade-spin. After about a month, i came THIS CLOSE to throwing the shaver out, until i realized what was happening. It took about 2 seconds to twirl-off the hairs, and then the shaver worked fine.

It's also easy to clean and has no battery that gets weak when low. And I read on line that so many people were vexed because the battery died within a year of the purchase. And when the battery is still alive, one has to play the game of charging it, and if you keep it on-charge for more than the specific charging time, the battery will be damaged. So much botheration - just because one wants to shave without a cord. All of these concerns are by-passed simply by plugging in the 6940 and shaving. There are sockets all over the house. The action on the 6940 is very good. Very quiet. Very sharp blades clip off the hair without pulling. Very light-weight in the hand. Easy to clean. We have a mini shop-vac in the house and I open up the head of the razor and and in 15 seconds the thing is clean as a whistle. No brushing. the only thing I would change is the electric cord. I like the way it feels in my hand, and the light weight makes it easy to use the trimmer and take a little extra time shaving.<br /><br />While I would rate this shaver as an extremely good value, it does have a few flaws, most of which are a function of being re-engineered to the absolute lowest possible cost of production while still performing the designed function. Here are a few of the design/production flaws that keep this from being a five star product (mainly mediocre fit & finish issues): 1) The cord is detachable and (as mentioned by others) quite short. It doesn't take very much to pull the cord out of the razor. I fixed this by using the hot glue gun to make the cord more or less permanently attached. Luckily my outlet is very close. About all that can be done for the length is reverse twist the spiral to reduce the tension. 2) The fit of the head on the body is a bit loose and it wiggles perceptibly. This was corrected by using a small amount of epoxy to build up the perimeter of the frame ever so slightly until the head fit snugly. 3) The materials seem to be &#34;extremely lightweight&#34; plastic (read: kinda cheap). These things keep this from being a five star product.<br /><br />My experience is that Norelco cutter heads last about 2 years. As others mentioned, it will be cheaper to replace the entire razor than the cutter head. At this price I will gladly consider this a two year razor, and am buying another one to have on hand when this on conks out or gets dull. I don't hesitate to recommend this razor.tter heads last about 2 years. As others mentioned, it will be cheaper to replace the entire razor than the cutter head. Because everyone has different thickness of hair and skin, I will try to describe mine:<br />(Disregard this review if you're hair is different)<br /><br />I have blond hair that's not extremely thick, but not thin either, I didn't start shaving until I was 19, and now that I'm 24 I only shave every couple of days. My skin just can't handle it. My face doesn't break out, but my neck is painful.<br /><br />So, I thought I'd switch to an electric razor to see if that would help. I thought it did at first, but the blade dulls quickly and if I made more than one pass on my neck it would get a razor burn. I could shave my face all day long with the electric razor and it felt fine. I never got a really close shave, but it was nice for the convenience of literally taking 30 seconds to shave my face without any mess. Still though, I was unsatisfied with the electric razor causing the rash on my neck and so I tried out Safety Razors.<br /><br />When I first heard about them, I thought it would be the same as using the standard 3-5 blade razors, boy was I wrong. I got a cheap badger hair brush, the Proraso sensitive skin shaving cream, an old safety razor (1942 Gillette) off of ebay and some Derby blades. NO MORE RASH. It takes a few times with the razor to learn how to hold it, but you don't run near the risk of getting a rash with it because it's just a single blade. I also don't worry about cutting myself with it. All in all it cost me about $30 to buy a new way of shaving and never worry about a rash again.

  550. For more years than I like to think about, I've used an electric razor every other day. It could have been every day but despite advertisers' claims, I never found one that shaved as close as a blade-- until now. Powering the razor from the AC mains is probably more expensive than a rechargeable battery, but the speed is constant and the design of the heads is such that you can get a very close, even shave. At a time when cartridge razor makers are insisting that you need more and more blades, it's refreshing to see a product that pretty much gets back to the basics. The cord is stiff when new, so I popped it out a couple times before figuring out that you can \\"pre-stretch\\" it a bit. I've heard that replacing the cutters annually as Norelco suggests is an expensive proposition, but IF they need replacing in a year, and are that expensive, I will consider buying a new razor-- the whole thing cost about the same as a year's worth of multiblade cartridges. Bottom line-- if you have been disappointed by electric razors in the past, try this one.
